{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_0129BR14iKRom3zYDtuazxfV","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01DtSnmXV5a1Rn5fWCix3wUf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Systems Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative configuration management system in Kubernetes that tracks field ownership through **managed fields**, enabling multiple controllers to safely co-manage resources without conflicts. The subsystem comprises three major parts: (1) **applyconfigurations**, auto-generated builder types that provide a fluent API for constructing apply patches; (2) **server-side field management**, which tracks field ownership and detects conflicts; and (3) **structured-merge-diff**, an external library implementing the merge algorithm that respects field ownership boundaries.\n\nThis guide explains how these components work together, the control flow from client through server, conflict resolution semantics, and operational considerations.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe Server-Side Apply subsystem solves a fundamental problem in declarative configuration management: **how do multiple parties (controllers, operators, users) safely modify the same resource without overwriting each other's changes?**\n\nBefore SSA, Kubernetes had no way to track field ownership. When controller A and user B both modified a Pod, their changes could overwrite each other unpredictably. SSA introduces field-level tracking via `metadata.managedFields`, creating a clear ownership model:\n\n- **Users/Controllers** declare intent: \"I want to own these fields\"\n- **Server tracks** who owns what through managed fields entries\n- **Server detects conflicts** when two managers disagree on field values\n- **Clients can force-apply** to claim disputed fields, with explicit acknowledgment\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`: Three-way merge algorithm implementing field ownership semantics\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery`: Base types, field validation, OpenAPI schema support\n- `k8s.io/apiserver`: HTTP handler infrastructure, admission chain, authorization\n- `k8s.io/client-go`: REST client, codec/serialization layer\n\n**Downstream Consumers:**\n- `kubectl apply` and imperative clients (use REST Patch API)\n- Control loops in controllers (use apply configurations)\n- Operators and automation tools\n- Users issuing PATCH requests with `application/apply-patch+yaml` or `application/apply-patch+cbor`\n\n**Not Included in SSA:**\n- Traditional PUT/POST (create/update): These use `Update` operation in managed fields\n- Three-way strategic merge patches: Handled separately in patch.go via Strategic Merge Patch (SMP)\n- Admission validation: Happens downstream in the admission chain\n- Storage/etcd: SSA writes JSON with embedded managed fields metadata\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Architecture Overview\n\n### High-Level Components\n\n```\n┌─ Client Layer ──────────────────────────────┐\n│  ApplyConfigurations (generated builders)   │\n│  client.REST.Patch(ApplyPatchType)         │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ PATCH + FieldManager header\n                   │ application/apply-patch+yaml|cbor\n                   ▼\n┌─ API Server HTTP Handler ───────────────────┐\n│  handlers.PatchResource()                   │\n│  ├─ ApplyPatcher (applies patch)           │\n│  ├─ FieldManager.Apply()                   │\n│  └─ Conflict detection & force-apply       │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ structured-merge-diff library\n                   │ conflict/merge algorithm\n                   ▼\n┌─ Field Management Core ─────────────────────┐\n│  managedfields.FieldManager                 │\n│  ├─ DecodeManaged Fields                   │\n│  ├─ StructuredMergeManager                 │\n│  ├─ Manager wrappers (CapManagers, etc)   │\n│  └─ Encode back to metadata.managedFields  │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ etcd storage\n                   ▼\n         Resource with embedded\n         metadata.managedFields\n```\n\n### Key Architectural Decisions\n\n1. **Field-level ownership tracking**: Each field can be owned by exactly one manager at a time. When a field changes owners, its history is preserved.\n\n2. **Merge happens at apply time**: The server doesn't track three-way state; it infers current state from existing managed fields and applies the patch. This keeps storage and computation simple.\n\n3. **Manager is a string identifier**: Includes API version, operation type, timestamp. Allows multiple versions/instances of the same controller to coexist.\n\n4. **Force-apply is explicit**: Users must pass `force: true` in `PatchOptions` to claim fields from other managers. This ensures intentionality.\n\n5. **Structured-merge-diff is external**: Kubernetes doesn't implement merge logic; it delegates to an external library. This decouples API semantics from implementation.\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 3.1 ApplyConfigurations: Generated Builders\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` (and resource-specific variants)\n\n**Purpose**: Provide a **fluent, type-safe API** for constructing apply patches without writing raw YAML/JSON.\n\n**Generated For**: Every API type that has `genclient` tag. Example: `DeploymentApplyConfiguration` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go`\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- **Constructor**: `Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration` — creates a new builder\n- **With-methods**: `WithReplicas(int) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration` — builder pattern, sets fields\n- **Extract methods**: `ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldManager)` — reverse operation, pulls an apply config from a resource\n\n**Example Usage**:\n```go\ndeployment := appsv1ac.Deployment(\"my-app\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        WithSelector(metav1ac.LabelSelector().\n            WithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})))\n\n// Create a REST request\nreq, err := apply.NewRequest(client, deployment).\n    Patch(types.ApplyYAMLPatchType).\n    Namespace(\"default\").\n    Resource(\"deployments\").\n    Name(\"my-app\").\n    Param(\"fieldManager\", \"my-controller\").\n    Do(ctx)\n```\n\n**Generation Process**:\n- Tool: `applyconfiguration-gen` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`\n- Input: API types with struct tags (`genclient`, `kubebuilder` annotations)\n- Output: One file per type in `applyconfigurations/` with typed builders\n- Key file: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/applyconfiguration.go` generates struct definitions, constructor, with-methods, and extract functions\n\n**Critical Design**:\n- Marked fields as `*pointer` to distinguish \"field was set\" from \"field is zero value\"\n- Embedded metadata types to preserve API structure\n- JSON tags omit empty values to minimize patch size\n- Extract functions parse `metadata.managedFields` to reconstruct what this manager owns\n\n### 3.2 HTTP Handler: PatchResource\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: HTTP entry point for PATCH requests. Dispatches to different patching mechanisms based on Content-Type.\n\n**Control Flow**:\n1. **Extract patch bytes** and `PatchOptions` from request\n2. **Validate patch type** (JSON/Merge/Strategic/Apply+YAML/Apply+CBOR)\n3. **Route to mechanism**:\n   - `ApplyYAMLPatchType` or `ApplyCBORPatchType` → `applyPatcher`\n   - `StrategicMergePatchType` → `smpPatcher`\n   - `MergePatchType` or `JSONPatchType` → `jsonPatcher`\n4. **Call `patchResource()` with `patcher` struct** containing:\n   - `mechanism` (interface with `applyPatchToCurrentObject`, `createNewObject`)\n   - `fieldManager` from `RequestScope` (instance of `managedfields.FieldManager`)\n   - `options` parsed from query params\n5. **Apply transformations**: `applyPatch`, `applyAdmission`, dedup owner references\n6. **Call `restPatcher.Update()`**: Persists via storage layer with `GuaranteedUpdate`\n7. **Return** serialized object\n\n**Critical Code Locations**:\n- Mechanism initialization: lines 656-690 in patch.go\n- Apply patch function: lines 500-538 (applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject)\n- Admission handling: lines 623-650 (patcher.applyAdmission)\n- Storage call: line 704 (restPatcher.Update)\n\n**Key Method: applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject**:\n```go\nfunc (p *applyPatcher) applyPatchToCurrentObject(requestContext context.Context, obj runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    force := *p.options.Force // true = claim fields from other managers\n    patchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{} // unmarshal patch body\n    obj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n    // return updated object with managed fields already merged\n}\n```\n\nThis delegates the actual merge to `managedfields.FieldManager.Apply()`.\n\n### 3.3 FieldManager: Core Merge Logic\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go` (wrapper) and `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` (implementation)\n\n**Responsibility**:\n- Decode `metadata.managedFields` from live object\n- Pass fields to structured-merge-diff for conflict detection and merge\n- Encode updated managed fields back into object\n\n**Public API**:\n```go\ntype FieldManager struct {\n    fieldManager Manager  // core merge logic\n    subresource  string   // \"status\", \"scale\", etc.\n}\n\n// Update: for non-apply operations (POST, PUT)\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) (object runtime.Object, err error)\n\n// Apply: for apply operations (PATCH with ApplyYAMLPatchType)\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(obj, patch runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error)\n```\n\n**Factory Function**: `NewDefaultFieldManager()` at line 36 in fieldmanager.go wraps a core manager with multiple decorator layers:\n```\nNewDefaultFieldManager\n├─ VersionCheckManager (validates API version)\n├─ LastAppliedUpdater (tracks \"last applied\" for backward compat)\n├─ LastAppliedManager (manages kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration)\n├─ ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager (optimization for non-apply operations)\n├─ CapManagersManager (limits manager count, merges old entries)\n├─ BuildManagerInfoManager (adds manager metadata like timestamp)\n├─ ManagedFieldsUpdater (updates object's managedFields)\n└─ StripMetaManager (removes managedFields from live object before processing)\n```\n\nEach decorator adds behavior:\n- **CapManagersManager**: Prevents unbounded growth of managedFields entries. Default limit is 10 Update operations; older ones are merged to keep storage bounded.\n- **BuildManagerInfoManager**: Adds timestamp and operation type (Apply vs Update) to manager entry\n- **LastAppliedManager**: Maintains `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation for backward compatibility with client-side apply\n\n### 3.4 Structured-Merge-Diff Integration\n\n**Location**: `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` (external library)\n\n**Responsibility**: Implements field-level merge and conflict detection.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n- **FieldPath**: Identifies a field, e.g., `[spec][replicas]` or `[metadata][labels][app]`\n- **ManagedFields**: Map of manager → set of fields they own\n- **Merge**: Combine three versions: live, patch, current managed state\n- **Conflicts**: When two managers claim the same field with different values\n\n**Kubernetes Integration**:\n- **TypeConverter** (in managedfields): Converts Kubernetes types to structured-merge-diff's internal representation\n- **GVKParser** in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/gvkparser.go`: Parses GroupVersionKind strings\n- **DecodeManagedFields** / **EncodeObjectManagedFields**: Serialize/deserialize managed fields from/to API objects\n\n**Conflict Detection**: In `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`:\n```go\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    // Convert low-level merge conflicts to API errors with field paths\n    // Returns HTTP 409 Conflict with per-field messages\n}\n```\n\n### 3.5 Managed Fields Validation in Admission\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Ensures admission controllers don't corrupt managed fields.\n\n**Mechanism**: Wrapper that:\n1. Captures managed fields **before** mutating admission runs\n2. Runs admission chain\n3. Validates managed fields **after** admission\n4. If invalid, **reverts** to pre-admission state and returns warning\n\n**Code**:\n```go\nfunc (admit *managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController) Admit(ctx context.Context, a admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    managedFieldsBeforeAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\n    if err := mutationInterface.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil {\n        return err\n    }\n    managedFieldsAfterAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\n    if err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n        objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission) // Revert!\n        warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", fmt.Sprintf(InvalidManagedFieldsAfterMutatingAdmissionWarningFormat, err.Error()))\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nThis protects the managed fields invariant even if buggy webhooks try to modify it.\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### Scenario: First Apply\n\n**Client**: User applies a Deployment using kubectl or client-go apply configuration.\n\n```bash\nkubectl apply -f deployment.yaml --field-manager=my-app\n```\n\n**Step 1: Client Construction**\n- kubectl/client reads YAML, constructs `DeploymentApplyConfiguration` object\n- Serializes to JSON (or CBOR if feature gate enabled)\n- Sets Content-Type: `application/apply-patch+yaml`\n- Sets query param: `fieldManager=my-app`\n\n**Step 2: HTTP Handler (patch.go:68-262)**\n```\nPatchResource() called with:\n- req.Header[\"Content-Type\"] = \"application/apply-patch+yaml\"\n- req.URL.Query()[\"fieldManager\"] = \"my-app\"\n- req.Body = {deployment spec as JSON}\n```\n\n- Validates patch type is supported (line 85-89)\n- Extracts PatchOptions from URL params (line 119)\n- Creates admission chain wrapper (line 200)\n- Instantiates `patcher` struct with `mechanism = applyPatcher` (line 672-673)\n\n**Step 3: Patch Application (patch.go:696-728)**\n- Calls `patchResource()`, which calls `restPatcher.Update()` with transformers:\n  1. `applyPatch`: Convert patch to object, call `fieldManager.Apply()`\n  2. `applyAdmission`: Run mutating admission\n  3. `dedupOwnerReferences`: Clean up duplicate owner references\n\n- `restPatcher.Update()` is `Store.Update()` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`\n- Uses `GuaranteedUpdate()`: Retries on conflict, calls transformers to compute desired state\n\n**Step 4: FieldManager.Apply() (managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:160+)**\n\nLive object doesn't exist yet. Flow:\n1. `decodeLiveOrNew()`: Tries to decode managed fields from live object (none exist)\n2. `f.fieldManager.Update()`: Passes to core manager (StructuredMergeManager from structured-merge-diff)\n3. Merge returns: new object + updated managed state\n4. `EncodeObjectManagedFields()`: Writes managed fields back into object's metadata\n\n**What managed fields look like after first apply**:\n```yaml\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: my-app\n    operation: Apply\n    apiVersion: apps/v1\n    time: \"2024-03-01T12:00:00Z\"\n    fieldsV1:\n      f:metadata:\n        f:name: {}\n        f:namespace: {}\n      f:spec:\n        f:replicas: {}\n        f:selector: {}\n        f:template: {}\n```\n\nEach field owned by `my-app` is listed in `fieldsV1` (internal structured representation of field ownership).\n\n**Step 5: Storage and Response**\n- `GuaranteedUpdate()` persists to etcd with managed fields\n- HTTP response: 200 OK (or 201 Created if first apply also created)\n- Body: Complete updated object with managed fields\n\n### Scenario: Conflict Resolution\n\n**Context**: User applied a Deployment (owns spec.replicas). Now a controller (HPA) wants to set replicas via traditional UPDATE.\n\n**What happens**:\n1. Controller does PUT request (Update operation, not Apply)\n2. Server calls `patchResource()` with transformers for non-apply path\n3. `fieldManager.Update()` is called (not Apply)\n4. StructuredMergeManager sees:\n   - Live object has `spec.replicas` owned by `my-app` (from apply)\n   - New object is setting `spec.replicas` to different value\n   - This is an Update by HPA controller\n5. Update operation **claims** the field. Managed fields entry for `my-app` is removed from that field.\n\n**Key behavior**: Non-apply updates always succeed and claim fields. This is different from Apply.\n\n### Scenario: Force Apply Under Conflict\n\n**Context**: User wants to reclaim spec.replicas from HPA controller.\n\n```bash\nkubectl apply deployment.yaml --field-manager=my-app --force-conflicts\n```\n\n**What happens**:\n1. ApplyPatchType request with `force=true` in PatchOptions\n2. `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()` passes `force=true` to `fieldManager.Apply()`\n3. StructuredMergeManager merge algorithm:\n   - Detects conflict: field currently owned by `hpa` controller\n   - With force=true: Accepts the conflict, claims field anyway\n   - Returns no conflict error\n4. Managed fields: `hpa` manager entry loses ownership of that field; `my-app` gains it\n5. Client gets 200 OK\n\n**Without force**: Server returns HTTP 409 Conflict with per-field details.\n\n### Scenario: Extract and Modify\n\n**Use case**: Read current state, extract managed fields for \"my-app\", modify, reapply.\n\n```go\nexisting, _ := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-app\", metav1.GetOptions{})\nconfig, _ := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(existing, \"my-app\") // from managed fields\nconfig.WithSpec(spec.WithReplicas(5)) // modify\napply.NewRequest(clientset, config).\n    Patch(types.ApplyYAMLPatchType).\n    Namespace(\"default\").\n    Resource(\"deployments\").\n    Name(\"my-app\").\n    Param(\"fieldManager\", \"my-app\").\n    Do(ctx)\n```\n\n**Flow**:\n1. `ExtractDeployment()` calls `managedfields.ExtractInto()` (extract.go:180)\n2. Parses `metadata.managedFields` for \"my-app\" entry\n3. Reconstructs DeploymentApplyConfiguration with only fields owned by \"my-app\"\n4. Client modifies, sends apply\n5. Server accepts with no conflicts (my-app re-applies same fields it already owns)\n\nThis pattern enables safe read-modify-apply loops.\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: ApplyConfigurations Generation in Detail\n\n### Generation Pipeline\n\n**Trigger**: Build process runs `applyconfiguration-gen` for each API group.\n\n**Command** (example):\n```bash\napplyconfiguration-gen \\\n  --input-dirs k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/apis/apps/v1 \\\n  --output-base /workspace/staging/src \\\n  --output-package-base k8s.io/client-go\n```\n\n### Generator Files\n\n**Main entry**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/main.go`\n\n**Key generators in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/`**:\n\n1. **applyconfiguration.go** (lines 39-150):\n   - `applyConfigurationGenerator.GenerateType()`: Main code generation loop\n   - Generates struct definition, constructor, with-methods, Extract functions\n   - Filters types by `genclient` tag\n\n2. **types.go**:\n   - Generates struct types for each API type\n   - Example: `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`\n\n3. **util.go**:\n   - Helper functions for naming, field handling\n   - Filters out special fields (ManagedFields, SelfLink per line 144)\n\n### Generated Struct Example\n\nFor an API type:\n```go\n// From k8s.io/api/apps/v1/types.go\ntype Deployment struct {\n    TypeMeta   `json:\",inline\"`\n    ObjectMeta `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec       DeploymentSpec `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status     DeploymentStatus `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nGenerator creates:\n```go\n// Generated in applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go\ntype DeploymentApplyConfiguration struct {\n    *metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *DeploymentStatusApplyConfiguration `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n\nfunc Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration {\n    b := &DeploymentApplyConfiguration{}\n    b.WithName(name)\n    b.WithNamespace(namespace)\n    b.WithKind(\"Deployment\")\n    b.WithAPIVersion(\"apps/v1\")\n    return b\n}\n\nfunc (b *DeploymentApplyConfiguration) WithSpec(spec *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration {\n    b.Spec = spec\n    return b\n}\n```\n\n### Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Pointer Fields**: Every field is a pointer (`*DeploymentSpec`). This distinguishes \"user set this to empty\" vs \"user didn't mention it\". Required for partial updates.\n\n2. **JSON Tags Omit Empty**: Pointers marshal with `omitempty`, so unset fields don't appear in the patch. Minimizes patch size.\n\n3. **Nested Types**: Recursive generation for embedded types (specs, metadata, etc.). Each gets its own builder.\n\n4. **Extract Functions**: Reverse operation that parses managed fields and reconstructs the apply configuration for a specific manager. Located at lines 56-100 in deployment.go example.\n\n5. **Blocklisted Fields**: Certain fields are never included:\n   - `ObjectMeta.ManagedFields`: Can't be client-set (generated from merge logic)\n   - `ObjectMeta.SelfLink`: Deprecated, filtered at line 148 in applyconfiguration.go\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Managed Fields and Conflict Handling\n\n### Managed Fields Entry Structure\n\n```yaml\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: \"my-controller\"\n    operation: \"Apply\"          # or \"Update\"\n    apiVersion: \"apps/v1\"\n    time: \"2024-03-01T12:00:00Z\"\n    fieldsV1:                    # Structured field representation\n      f:spec:\n        f:replicas: {}\n        f:template:\n          f:spec:\n                f:containers:\n                  k:{\"name\":\"app\"}:\n                    f:image: {}\n```\n\n**Manager String**: Identifies the client making the request. Typically includes API version and operation type for deduplication.\n\n**Operation**:\n- `Apply`: From PATCH with ApplyYAMLPatchType; idempotent\n- `Update`: From PUT/POST; overrides previous values\n\n**FieldsV1**: Internal representation using structured-merge-diff's fieldpath.Path API. Each field path is tracked separately.\n\n### Conflict Detection Algorithm\n\n**Trigger**: When `FieldManager.Apply()` is called with `force=false`:\n\n```go\n// managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:160+\nobj, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)\nif conflict, isConflict := err.(*merge.Conflicts); isConflict && !force {\n    return nil, internal.NewConflictError(conflict)\n}\n```\n\n**Detection**: Delegated to structured-merge-diff:\n1. Decode managed fields from live object (knows current ownership)\n2. For each field in patch:\n   - If owned by a different manager AND value differs → conflict\n3. Return list of conflicting paths and their owners\n\n**Example**:\n- Live: `spec.replicas=3, owned by hpa`\n- Patch: `spec.replicas=5, sent by my-app`\n- Conflict: Path `[spec][replicas]`, manager `hpa`\n\n**Conflict Error**: HTTP 409 with causes per `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"code\": 409,\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      {\n        \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\",\n        \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"hpa\\\"\",\n        \"field\": \"spec.replicas\"\n      }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Force Apply Semantics\n\n**PatchOptions.Force = true** means: \"I acknowledge conflicts and claim disputed fields.\"\n\n**Server behavior**:\n1. Ignores conflicts during merge\n2. Removes conflicting fields from other managers' entries\n3. Adds those fields to requesting manager's entry\n4. Returns 200 OK with modified object\n\n**Critical caveat**: Force apply is **not** a three-way merge. The patch completely replaces fields, not merges them. If patch omits a list, entire list is deleted.\n\n### Backward Compatibility: Last-Applied-Configuration\n\n**Purpose**: kubectl apply traditionally stored `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` to compute three-way diffs (local → server → last-known). SSA renders this obsolete but maintains it for compatibility.\n\n**Manager**: `LastAppliedManager` wrapper in managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go\n\n**Behavior**:\n- When Apply operation succeeds, annotation is updated to the patch that was applied\n- Non-Apply operations (PUT) don't modify it\n- Useful for clients that haven't migrated to native SSA\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Custom FieldManager Wrappers\n\n**Hook Point**: `NewDefaultFieldManager()` constructor chain at lines 56-74 in managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go.\n\n**Current Wrappers**:\n- **VersionCheckManager**: Validates APIVersion matches expected\n- **LastAppliedUpdater**: Maintains last-applied-configuration annotation\n- **ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager**: Optimization to skip merge processing for non-apply operations with probability DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability (1.0 by default)\n- **CapManagersManager**: Limits number of tracked managers to prevent unbounded growth\n\n**Extension Pattern**:\n```go\ntype CustomManager struct {\n    wrapped Manager\n}\n\nfunc (m *CustomManager) Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (object runtime.Object, managed Managed, err error) {\n    // custom logic before\n    object, managed, err = m.wrapped.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)\n    // custom logic after\n    return\n}\n```\n\n**Use Case**: Audit field changes, enforce naming conventions, inject standard labels/annotations.\n\n### 7.2 TypeConverter Customization\n\n**Location**: managedfields/typeconverter.go\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    Convert(obj interface{}, typeFQN string) (*value.Value, error)\n    ObjectToTyped(obj runtime.Object) (*value.Value, error)\n    TypedToObject(val *value.Value) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Default**: Uses `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter` to convert typed objects to unstructured maps.\n\n**Extension**: CRDs can provide custom converters to handle non-standard types.\n\n### 7.3 Schema Definition: OpenAPI Integration\n\n**Purpose**: Structured-merge-diff uses OpenAPI schemas to understand field types (maps, lists, scalars). This enables proper merge semantics:\n- Map fields: Merge recursively\n- List fields with merge keys: Reorder/dedup by key\n- Scalar fields: Replace atomically\n\n**In Kubernetes**:\n- Built-in types: Schema inferred from Go structs (via OpenAPI gen)\n- CRDs: Schema defined in `spec.validation.openAPIV3Schema`\n\n**If schema missing**: Fallback to \"unknown type\" merge (treats all values as scalars, no recursion).\n\n### 7.4 Managed Fields Reset: Field Filters\n\n**Location**: managedfields/fieldmanager.go:36-52 (resetFields parameter)\n\n**Purpose**: On resource creation, exclude certain fields from being tracked (e.g., status subresources).\n\n**API**:\n```go\nresetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter\n\n// Example: status fields not tracked on create\nresetFields[v1.APIVersion] = filter matching \"status\" fields\n```\n\n**Effect**: Fields in resetFields start unowned; any manager setting them later claims them cleanly.\n\n**Use Case**: Status subresources should be owned by status controllers, not regular managers.\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs\n\n### 8.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Managed Fields Corruption by Admission\n\n**Problem**: Mutating admission webhooks may modify objects in ways that corrupt managed fields.\n\n**Mitigation** (fieldmanager/admission.go): Wrapper validates managed fields after each admission pass. If invalid, **reverts** to pre-admission state and adds warning.\n\n**Limitation**: Validation only catches structural corruption (invalid JSON in fieldsV1). Webhooks can still add fields that bypass field ownership checks.\n\n#### Unbounded Manager Count\n\n**Problem**: If many different clients apply to same resource, managed fields grows without bound.\n\n**Mitigation** (CapManagersManager): Limit to DefaultMaxUpdateManagers=10. Older Update entries are merged (combined).\n\n**Limitation**: Compressed history loses field ownership details for old managers. After compression, can't extract precise previous configurations.\n\n**Impact**: If >10 controllers touch a resource, some history is lost.\n\n#### Conflict on Apply with Small Patch\n\n**Problem**: User applies a partial patch that conflicts with another controller's full specification.\n\n**Example**:\n```yaml\n# Controller A owns full Pod spec\n# User tries to apply just image: \"v2\"\n# But controller A had image: \"v1\"\n# Conflict on image!\n```\n\n**Solution**: Force-apply, but only if intentional.\n\n**Limitation**: Force-apply is all-or-nothing. Can't force specific fields.\n\n#### Schema Mismatch with CRDs\n\n**Problem**: CRD schema changes (list field becomes map), but old managed fields still reference old structure.\n\n**Mitigation**: If schema can't be found during merge, falls back to scalar merge (no recursion).\n\n**Limitation**: Older managed fields entries for pre-schema-change structure become stale.\n\n#### Lost Updates via GuaranteedUpdate Retry\n\n**Problem**: HTTP request timeout during GuaranteedUpdate retry loop.\n\n**Mitigation** (patch.go:734-736): If timeout error received, server can't guarantee whether object was persisted.\n\n**Behavior**: Returns 504 Gateway Timeout. Client must retry with awareness that object may have been created.\n\n**Limitation**: No way to know if partial application succeeded. Requires idempotent apply semantics.\n\n### 8.2 Limits\n\n| Limit | Value | Location | Note |\n|-------|-------|----------|------|\n| Max JSON Patch operations | 10,000 | patch.go:64 | Per RFC 6902 |\n| Max Update managers | 10 | managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:35 | Older entries merged |\n| Max request body size | Configurable (default 3MB) | handlers/patch.go:110 | Via apiserver flag |\n| Max field path depth | Unbounded | structured-merge-diff | Theoretical limit depends on memory |\n| Managed fields JSON size | Unbounded | Storage | Large numbers of managers → larger objects |\n\n### 8.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Field-Level vs. Resource-Level Ownership\n\n**Choice**: Kubernetes uses field-level tracking.\n\n**Pro**: Multiple controllers can co-manage same resource at different fields. HPA sets replicas, user manages selector.\n\n**Con**: Adds complexity, requires schema understanding, merge logic more intricate.\n\n**Alternative**: Resource-level (last-write-wins). Simpler but forces exclusive ownership.\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Three-Way Merge vs. Two-Way\n\n**Choice**: Kubernetes uses two-way merge (current state + patch), reconstructs previous state from managed fields.\n\n**Pro**: Doesn't require client to send three-way state, reduces API complexity.\n\n**Con**: Reconstructed \"previous\" state may be incomplete (other managers may have modified fields).\n\n**Example**:\n```\nLive state:  replicas=5, owned by HPA\nPatch:       replicas=3, sent by user\nReconstructed \"previous\" from managed fields: HPA owns replicas (assumed value is 5)\nMerge result: Conflict (HPA disagrees with user's 3)\n```\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Force-Apply Atomicity\n\n**Choice**: Force-apply claims all fields in patch, not selective.\n\n**Pro**: Simple to implement, clear semantics.\n\n**Con**: Can't force-apply specific fields, must accept all-or-nothing.\n\n**Workaround**: Extract, modify specific fields, reapply (avoids conflicts).\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Manager String Format\n\n**Choice**: Opaque JSON string containing { manager, operation, apiVersion }.\n\n**Pro**: Extensible, can add fields for future needs.\n\n**Con**: Not human-readable, requires JSON parsing to inspect.\n\n**Alternative**: Structured tuple (manager, op, version).\n\n---\n\n## Part 9: Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Performance Impact\n\n#### Apply Patch Processing\n\n**Cost**: Structured-merge-diff three-way merge is O(n) in live object size and patch size.\n\n**Optimization 1** (ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager): For non-Apply operations, skip merge if fields are likely untouched (configurable probability, default 100% skip).\n\n**Optimization 2** (CapManagersManager): Merge old Update entries to keep manager count low.\n\n**Optimization 3** (patch.go:713-726): If object too large, retry after removing managedFields. Managed fields can be >100KB on large objects with many managers.\n\n**Result**: First few applies are slow (merge), subsequent non-apply updates are fast (skip).\n\n#### Managed Fields Storage Overhead\n\n**Typical**: 0.5-2KB per managed entry, depends on number of fields tracked.\n\n**Large scale**: 10 managers × 500 fields average = ~5KB managed fields metadata.\n\n**Impact**: Cluster with 10,000 Pods × 5KB = 50MB total managed fields metadata in etcd.\n\n**Mitigation**: Regularly delete old/unused controllers to keep manager count low.\n\n### 9.2 Debugging and Troubleshooting\n\n#### Inspect Managed Fields\n\n```bash\nkubectl get pod <name> -o yaml | grep -A 50 \"managedFields:\"\n```\n\nShows which manager owns which fields, when last modified.\n\n#### Extract Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Extract what \"my-app\" manager owns\nkubectl get deployment <name> -o yaml | \\\n  jq '.metadata.managedFields[] | select(.manager==\"my-app\")'\n```\n\nHelps understand what a controller thinks it should own.\n\n#### Conflict Resolution\n\n```bash\n# Check conflict details\nkubectl apply -f config.yaml 2>&1 | grep \"conflict with\"\n\n# Force apply to claim fields\nkubectl apply -f config.yaml --field-manager=my-app --force-conflicts\n```\n\n#### Manager Cleanup\n\n```bash\n# List active managers on a resource\nkubectl patch deployment <name> --type='json' -p='[{\"op\":\"test\",\"path\":\"/metadata/managedFields\"}]'\n\n# Manually clear stale manager (CAUTION: only if manager is truly abandoned)\nkubectl patch deployment <name> --type='json' \\\n  -p='[{\"op\":\"remove\",\"path\":\"/metadata/managedFields/0\"}]'\n```\n\n### 9.3 Migration Considerations\n\n#### From Traditional PUT/POST to Apply\n\n**Challenge**: Existing resources have no managed fields. First apply sees all fields as unowned.\n\n**Mitigation**: Initial apply claims all fields:\n```bash\nkubectl apply -f existing-resource.yaml --field-manager=new-manager --force-conflicts\n```\n\n**Result**: Migrates resource to SSA model.\n\n#### From Client-Side Apply to Server-Side Apply\n\n**Tool**: `kubectl apply --server-side` (requires cluster v1.18+).\n\n**Process**:\n1. Read current state (live object + managedFields)\n2. Extract last-applied-configuration annotation\n3. Compute three-way diff (last → live → desired)\n4. Send as apply PATCH\n5. Server merges with other manager changes\n\n**Compatibility**: Server-side apply is backward compatible; old resources automatically gain managed fields.\n\n#### Multi-Version Controller Rollout\n\n**Scenario**: Rolling out new version of controller with different field ownership.\n\n**Approach**:\n1. Old and new versions coexist (different manager strings, e.g., \"my-controller:v1\" vs \"my-controller:v2\")\n2. Each manages same fields but with different manager names\n3. On rollout: New version applies same fields, old version's entries become stale\n4. After stabilization: Run cleanup to merge old manager entries\n\n**Caution**: If both versions apply simultaneously, conflicts arise until old version is deleted.\n\n### 9.4 Reliability and Data Consistency\n\n#### Idempotency\n\n**Property**: Applying same configuration multiple times produces same result.\n\n**Guaranteed by**: Apply with same field values always succeeds (no conflict on identical fields).\n\n**Exception**: External changes (e.g., HPA sets replicas differently) cause conflicts on next apply.\n\n**Implication**: Controllers can safely retry apply on transient errors without duplicating side effects.\n\n#### Observability\n\n**What's Tracked**:\n- Each managed field's owner, timestamp, operation\n- **Not tracked**: When fields were set, intermediate values, change history\n\n**Limitation**: Can't audit \"who changed field X on date Y\" without reading etcd snapshots.\n\n**Alternative**: Use Kubernetes audit logging (separate system) to track API requests.\n\n#### Quota and Accounting\n\n**Managed Fields Count Toward**:\n- Resource size (quota.requests.storage)\n- **Not counted separately**: No per-manager quota\n\n**Implication**: Unbounded managers on single object can bloat resource size, potentially hitting quotas.\n\n**Mitigation**: Enforce application-level manager naming standards, cleanup old managers.\n\n---\n\n## Part 10: Critical File Map and Key Locations\n\n### Core SSA Implementation\n\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | 68-262 | HTTP handler for PATCH requests; routes to patching mechanisms |\n| Conclusion\n\nServer-Side Apply is a sophisticated system that enables safe, declarative configuration management in Kubernetes by tracking field ownership at the API server level. Its key innovation is moving from \"last-write-wins\" to \"field-level ownership,\" allowing multiple controllers to coexist on the same resource.\n\nThe subsystem achieves this through:\n\n1. **ApplyConfigurations**: Type-safe builders generated for every API type, enabling clients to construct apply patches without raw YAML\n2. **FieldManager**: Orchestrates merge logic, decodes/encodes managed fields, wraps with optimization and validation layers\n3. **Structured-Merge-Diff**: External library implementing field ownership semantics and conflict detection\n4. **HTTP Handler**: Routes PATCH requests with apply content-type to the merge pipeline\n5. **Managed Fields Metadata**: Tracks per-field ownership, operation type, and timestamp in API objects\n\nUnderstanding this system enables:\n- Effective multi-controller resource management\n- Predictable conflict resolution\n- Safe schema evolution\n- Operational debugging of ownership disputes\n- Integration of new controllers without breaking existing ones\n\nThe design prioritizes **safety over simplicity**: field-level tracking and structured merge logic add complexity but prevent whole categories of data loss and ownership conflicts that plagued earlier Kubernetes versions.\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1868,"cache_read_input_tokens":67154,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1868},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5faf5c1a-646f-4195-bbb5-222fd18965f6","uuid":"76a82d73-2c5f-4fab-a71a-d8d1ef7999a5"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01DtSnmXV5a1Rn5fWCix3wUf","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /workspace/documentation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"5faf5c1a-646f-4195-bbb5-222fd18965f6","uuid":"b016c8c7-2e4e-4406-bcea-1d37a5973a06","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply and ApplyConfigurations: A Deep Systems Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative configuration management system in Kubernetes that tracks field ownership through **managed fields**, enabling multiple controllers to safely co-manage resources without conflicts. The subsystem comprises three major parts: (1) **applyconfigurations**, auto-generated builder types that provide a fluent API for constructing apply patches; (2) **server-side field management**, which tracks field ownership and detects conflicts; and (3) **structured-merge-diff**, an external library implementing the merge algorithm that respects field ownership boundaries.\n\nThis guide explains how these components work together, the control flow from client through server, conflict resolution semantics, and operational considerations.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe Server-Side Apply subsystem solves a fundamental problem in declarative configuration management: **how do multiple parties (controllers, operators, users) safely modify the same resource without overwriting each other's changes?**\n\nBefore SSA, Kubernetes had no way to track field ownership. When controller A and user B both modified a Pod, their changes could overwrite each other unpredictably. SSA introduces field-level tracking via `metadata.managedFields`, creating a clear ownership model:\n\n- **Users/Controllers** declare intent: \"I want to own these fields\"\n- **Server tracks** who owns what through managed fields entries\n- **Server detects conflicts** when two managers disagree on field values\n- **Clients can force-apply** to claim disputed fields, with explicit acknowledgment\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6`: Three-way merge algorithm implementing field ownership semantics\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery`: Base types, field validation, OpenAPI schema support\n- `k8s.io/apiserver`: HTTP handler infrastructure, admission chain, authorization\n- `k8s.io/client-go`: REST client, codec/serialization layer\n\n**Downstream Consumers:**\n- `kubectl apply` and imperative clients (use REST Patch API)\n- Control loops in controllers (use apply configurations)\n- Operators and automation tools\n- Users issuing PATCH requests with `application/apply-patch+yaml` or `application/apply-patch+cbor`\n\n**Not Included in SSA:**\n- Traditional PUT/POST (create/update): These use `Update` operation in managed fields\n- Three-way strategic merge patches: Handled separately in patch.go via Strategic Merge Patch (SMP)\n- Admission validation: Happens downstream in the admission chain\n- Storage/etcd: SSA writes JSON with embedded managed fields metadata\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Architecture Overview\n\n### High-Level Components\n\n```\n┌─ Client Layer ──────────────────────────────┐\n│  ApplyConfigurations (generated builders)   │\n│  client.REST.Patch(ApplyPatchType)         │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ PATCH + FieldManager header\n                   │ application/apply-patch+yaml|cbor\n                   ▼\n┌─ API Server HTTP Handler ───────────────────┐\n│  handlers.PatchResource()                   │\n│  ├─ ApplyPatcher (applies patch)           │\n│  ├─ FieldManager.Apply()                   │\n│  └─ Conflict detection & force-apply       │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ structured-merge-diff library\n                   │ conflict/merge algorithm\n                   ▼\n┌─ Field Management Core ─────────────────────┐\n│  managedfields.FieldManager                 │\n│  ├─ DecodeManaged Fields                   │\n│  ├─ StructuredMergeManager                 │\n│  ├─ Manager wrappers (CapManagers, etc)   │\n│  └─ Encode back to metadata.managedFields  │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │ etcd storage\n                   ▼\n         Resource with embedded\n         metadata.managedFields\n```\n\n### Key Architectural Decisions\n\n1. **Field-level ownership tracking**: Each field can be owned by exactly one manager at a time. When a field changes owners, its history is preserved.\n\n2. **Merge happens at apply time**: The server doesn't track three-way state; it infers current state from existing managed fields and applies the patch. This keeps storage and computation simple.\n\n3. **Manager is a string identifier**: Includes API version, operation type, timestamp. Allows multiple versions/instances of the same controller to coexist.\n\n4. **Force-apply is explicit**: Users must pass `force: true` in `PatchOptions` to claim fields from other managers. This ensures intentionality.\n\n5. **Structured-merge-diff is external**: Kubernetes doesn't implement merge logic; it delegates to an external library. This decouples API semantics from implementation.\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Key Components and Responsibilities\n\n### 3.1 ApplyConfigurations: Generated Builders\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` (and resource-specific variants)\n\n**Purpose**: Provide a **fluent, type-safe API** for constructing apply patches without writing raw YAML/JSON.\n\n**Generated For**: Every API type that has `genclient` tag. Example: `DeploymentApplyConfiguration` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go`\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- **Constructor**: `Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration` — creates a new builder\n- **With-methods**: `WithReplicas(int) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration` — builder pattern, sets fields\n- **Extract methods**: `ExtractDeployment(deployment, fieldManager)` — reverse operation, pulls an apply config from a resource\n\n**Example Usage**:\n```go\ndeployment := appsv1ac.Deployment(\"my-app\", \"default\").\n    WithSpec(appsv1ac.DeploymentSpec().\n        WithReplicas(3).\n        WithSelector(metav1ac.LabelSelector().\n            WithMatchLabels(map[string]string{\"app\": \"my-app\"})))\n\n// Create a REST request\nreq, err := apply.NewRequest(client, deployment).\n    Patch(types.ApplyYAMLPatchType).\n    Namespace(\"default\").\n    Resource(\"deployments\").\n    Name(\"my-app\").\n    Param(\"fieldManager\", \"my-controller\").\n    Do(ctx)\n```\n\n**Generation Process**:\n- Tool: `applyconfiguration-gen` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/`\n- Input: API types with struct tags (`genclient`, `kubebuilder` annotations)\n- Output: One file per type in `applyconfigurations/` with typed builders\n- Key file: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/applyconfiguration.go` generates struct definitions, constructor, with-methods, and extract functions\n\n**Critical Design**:\n- Marked fields as `*pointer` to distinguish \"field was set\" from \"field is zero value\"\n- Embedded metadata types to preserve API structure\n- JSON tags omit empty values to minimize patch size\n- Extract functions parse `metadata.managedFields` to reconstruct what this manager owns\n\n### 3.2 HTTP Handler: PatchResource\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: HTTP entry point for PATCH requests. Dispatches to different patching mechanisms based on Content-Type.\n\n**Control Flow**:\n1. **Extract patch bytes** and `PatchOptions` from request\n2. **Validate patch type** (JSON/Merge/Strategic/Apply+YAML/Apply+CBOR)\n3. **Route to mechanism**:\n   - `ApplyYAMLPatchType` or `ApplyCBORPatchType` → `applyPatcher`\n   - `StrategicMergePatchType` → `smpPatcher`\n   - `MergePatchType` or `JSONPatchType` → `jsonPatcher`\n4. **Call `patchResource()` with `patcher` struct** containing:\n   - `mechanism` (interface with `applyPatchToCurrentObject`, `createNewObject`)\n   - `fieldManager` from `RequestScope` (instance of `managedfields.FieldManager`)\n   - `options` parsed from query params\n5. **Apply transformations**: `applyPatch`, `applyAdmission`, dedup owner references\n6. **Call `restPatcher.Update()`**: Persists via storage layer with `GuaranteedUpdate`\n7. **Return** serialized object\n\n**Critical Code Locations**:\n- Mechanism initialization: lines 656-690 in patch.go\n- Apply patch function: lines 500-538 (applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject)\n- Admission handling: lines 623-650 (patcher.applyAdmission)\n- Storage call: line 704 (restPatcher.Update)\n\n**Key Method: applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject**:\n```go\nfunc (p *applyPatcher) applyPatchToCurrentObject(requestContext context.Context, obj runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    force := *p.options.Force // true = claim fields from other managers\n    patchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{} // unmarshal patch body\n    obj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n    // return updated object with managed fields already merged\n}\n```\n\nThis delegates the actual merge to `managedfields.FieldManager.Apply()`.\n\n### 3.3 FieldManager: Core Merge Logic\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go` (wrapper) and `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` (implementation)\n\n**Responsibility**:\n- Decode `metadata.managedFields` from live object\n- Pass fields to structured-merge-diff for conflict detection and merge\n- Encode updated managed fields back into object\n\n**Public API**:\n```go\ntype FieldManager struct {\n    fieldManager Manager  // core merge logic\n    subresource  string   // \"status\", \"scale\", etc.\n}\n\n// Update: for non-apply operations (POST, PUT)\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, manager string) (object runtime.Object, err error)\n\n// Apply: for apply operations (PATCH with ApplyYAMLPatchType)\nfunc (f *FieldManager) Apply(obj, patch runtime.Object, manager string, force bool) (object runtime.Object, err error)\n```\n\n**Factory Function**: `NewDefaultFieldManager()` at line 36 in fieldmanager.go wraps a core manager with multiple decorator layers:\n```\nNewDefaultFieldManager\n├─ VersionCheckManager (validates API version)\n├─ LastAppliedUpdater (tracks \"last applied\" for backward compat)\n├─ LastAppliedManager (manages kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration)\n├─ ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager (optimization for non-apply operations)\n├─ CapManagersManager (limits manager count, merges old entries)\n├─ BuildManagerInfoManager (adds manager metadata like timestamp)\n├─ ManagedFieldsUpdater (updates object's managedFields)\n└─ StripMetaManager (removes managedFields from live object before processing)\n```\n\nEach decorator adds behavior:\n- **CapManagersManager**: Prevents unbounded growth of managedFields entries. Default limit is 10 Update operations; older ones are merged to keep storage bounded.\n- **BuildManagerInfoManager**: Adds timestamp and operation type (Apply vs Update) to manager entry\n- **LastAppliedManager**: Maintains `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` annotation for backward compatibility with client-side apply\n\n### 3.4 Structured-Merge-Diff Integration\n\n**Location**: `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` (external library)\n\n**Responsibility**: Implements field-level merge and conflict detection.\n\n**Key Concepts**:\n- **FieldPath**: Identifies a field, e.g., `[spec][replicas]` or `[metadata][labels][app]`\n- **ManagedFields**: Map of manager → set of fields they own\n- **Merge**: Combine three versions: live, patch, current managed state\n- **Conflicts**: When two managers claim the same field with different values\n\n**Kubernetes Integration**:\n- **TypeConverter** (in managedfields): Converts Kubernetes types to structured-merge-diff's internal representation\n- **GVKParser** in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/gvkparser.go`: Parses GroupVersionKind strings\n- **DecodeManagedFields** / **EncodeObjectManagedFields**: Serialize/deserialize managed fields from/to API objects\n\n**Conflict Detection**: In `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`:\n```go\nfunc NewConflictError(conflicts merge.Conflicts) *errors.StatusError {\n    // Convert low-level merge conflicts to API errors with field paths\n    // Returns HTTP 409 Conflict with per-field messages\n}\n```\n\n### 3.5 Managed Fields Validation in Admission\n\n**Location**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Ensures admission controllers don't corrupt managed fields.\n\n**Mechanism**: Wrapper that:\n1. Captures managed fields **before** mutating admission runs\n2. Runs admission chain\n3. Validates managed fields **after** admission\n4. If invalid, **reverts** to pre-admission state and returns warning\n\n**Code**:\n```go\nfunc (admit *managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController) Admit(ctx context.Context, a admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    managedFieldsBeforeAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\n    if err := mutationInterface.Admit(ctx, a, o); err != nil {\n        return err\n    }\n    managedFieldsAfterAdmission := objectMeta.GetManagedFields()\n    if err := managedfields.ValidateManagedFields(managedFieldsAfterAdmission); err != nil {\n        objectMeta.SetManagedFields(managedFieldsBeforeAdmission) // Revert!\n        warning.AddWarning(ctx, \"\", fmt.Sprintf(InvalidManagedFieldsAfterMutatingAdmissionWarningFormat, err.Error()))\n    }\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\nThis protects the managed fields invariant even if buggy webhooks try to modify it.\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### Scenario: First Apply\n\n**Client**: User applies a Deployment using kubectl or client-go apply configuration.\n\n```bash\nkubectl apply -f deployment.yaml --field-manager=my-app\n```\n\n**Step 1: Client Construction**\n- kubectl/client reads YAML, constructs `DeploymentApplyConfiguration` object\n- Serializes to JSON (or CBOR if feature gate enabled)\n- Sets Content-Type: `application/apply-patch+yaml`\n- Sets query param: `fieldManager=my-app`\n\n**Step 2: HTTP Handler (patch.go:68-262)**\n```\nPatchResource() called with:\n- req.Header[\"Content-Type\"] = \"application/apply-patch+yaml\"\n- req.URL.Query()[\"fieldManager\"] = \"my-app\"\n- req.Body = {deployment spec as JSON}\n```\n\n- Validates patch type is supported (line 85-89)\n- Extracts PatchOptions from URL params (line 119)\n- Creates admission chain wrapper (line 200)\n- Instantiates `patcher` struct with `mechanism = applyPatcher` (line 672-673)\n\n**Step 3: Patch Application (patch.go:696-728)**\n- Calls `patchResource()`, which calls `restPatcher.Update()` with transformers:\n  1. `applyPatch`: Convert patch to object, call `fieldManager.Apply()`\n  2. `applyAdmission`: Run mutating admission\n  3. `dedupOwnerReferences`: Clean up duplicate owner references\n\n- `restPatcher.Update()` is `Store.Update()` in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/registry/generic/registry/store.go`\n- Uses `GuaranteedUpdate()`: Retries on conflict, calls transformers to compute desired state\n\n**Step 4: FieldManager.Apply() (managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:160+)**\n\nLive object doesn't exist yet. Flow:\n1. `decodeLiveOrNew()`: Tries to decode managed fields from live object (none exist)\n2. `f.fieldManager.Update()`: Passes to core manager (StructuredMergeManager from structured-merge-diff)\n3. Merge returns: new object + updated managed state\n4. `EncodeObjectManagedFields()`: Writes managed fields back into object's metadata\n\n**What managed fields look like after first apply**:\n```yaml\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: my-app\n    operation: Apply\n    apiVersion: apps/v1\n    time: \"2024-03-01T12:00:00Z\"\n    fieldsV1:\n      f:metadata:\n        f:name: {}\n        f:namespace: {}\n      f:spec:\n        f:replicas: {}\n        f:selector: {}\n        f:template: {}\n```\n\nEach field owned by `my-app` is listed in `fieldsV1` (internal structured representation of field ownership).\n\n**Step 5: Storage and Response**\n- `GuaranteedUpdate()` persists to etcd with managed fields\n- HTTP response: 200 OK (or 201 Created if first apply also created)\n- Body: Complete updated object with managed fields\n\n### Scenario: Conflict Resolution\n\n**Context**: User applied a Deployment (owns spec.replicas). Now a controller (HPA) wants to set replicas via traditional UPDATE.\n\n**What happens**:\n1. Controller does PUT request (Update operation, not Apply)\n2. Server calls `patchResource()` with transformers for non-apply path\n3. `fieldManager.Update()` is called (not Apply)\n4. StructuredMergeManager sees:\n   - Live object has `spec.replicas` owned by `my-app` (from apply)\n   - New object is setting `spec.replicas` to different value\n   - This is an Update by HPA controller\n5. Update operation **claims** the field. Managed fields entry for `my-app` is removed from that field.\n\n**Key behavior**: Non-apply updates always succeed and claim fields. This is different from Apply.\n\n### Scenario: Force Apply Under Conflict\n\n**Context**: User wants to reclaim spec.replicas from HPA controller.\n\n```bash\nkubectl apply deployment.yaml --field-manager=my-app --force-conflicts\n```\n\n**What happens**:\n1. ApplyPatchType request with `force=true` in PatchOptions\n2. `applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject()` passes `force=true` to `fieldManager.Apply()`\n3. StructuredMergeManager merge algorithm:\n   - Detects conflict: field currently owned by `hpa` controller\n   - With force=true: Accepts the conflict, claims field anyway\n   - Returns no conflict error\n4. Managed fields: `hpa` manager entry loses ownership of that field; `my-app` gains it\n5. Client gets 200 OK\n\n**Without force**: Server returns HTTP 409 Conflict with per-field details.\n\n### Scenario: Extract and Modify\n\n**Use case**: Read current state, extract managed fields for \"my-app\", modify, reapply.\n\n```go\nexisting, _ := clientset.AppsV1().Deployments(\"default\").Get(ctx, \"my-app\", metav1.GetOptions{})\nconfig, _ := appsv1ac.ExtractDeployment(existing, \"my-app\") // from managed fields\nconfig.WithSpec(spec.WithReplicas(5)) // modify\napply.NewRequest(clientset, config).\n    Patch(types.ApplyYAMLPatchType).\n    Namespace(\"default\").\n    Resource(\"deployments\").\n    Name(\"my-app\").\n    Param(\"fieldManager\", \"my-app\").\n    Do(ctx)\n```\n\n**Flow**:\n1. `ExtractDeployment()` calls `managedfields.ExtractInto()` (extract.go:180)\n2. Parses `metadata.managedFields` for \"my-app\" entry\n3. Reconstructs DeploymentApplyConfiguration with only fields owned by \"my-app\"\n4. Client modifies, sends apply\n5. Server accepts with no conflicts (my-app re-applies same fields it already owns)\n\nThis pattern enables safe read-modify-apply loops.\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: ApplyConfigurations Generation in Detail\n\n### Generation Pipeline\n\n**Trigger**: Build process runs `applyconfiguration-gen` for each API group.\n\n**Command** (example):\n```bash\napplyconfiguration-gen \\\n  --input-dirs k8s.io/kubernetes/pkg/apis/apps/v1 \\\n  --output-base /workspace/staging/src \\\n  --output-package-base k8s.io/client-go\n```\n\n### Generator Files\n\n**Main entry**: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/main.go`\n\n**Key generators in `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/`**:\n\n1. **applyconfiguration.go** (lines 39-150):\n   - `applyConfigurationGenerator.GenerateType()`: Main code generation loop\n   - Generates struct definition, constructor, with-methods, Extract functions\n   - Filters types by `genclient` tag\n\n2. **types.go**:\n   - Generates struct types for each API type\n   - Example: `DeploymentApplyConfiguration`\n\n3. **util.go**:\n   - Helper functions for naming, field handling\n   - Filters out special fields (ManagedFields, SelfLink per line 144)\n\n### Generated Struct Example\n\nFor an API type:\n```go\n// From k8s.io/api/apps/v1/types.go\ntype Deployment struct {\n    TypeMeta   `json:\",inline\"`\n    ObjectMeta `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec       DeploymentSpec `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status     DeploymentStatus `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n```\n\nGenerator creates:\n```go\n// Generated in applyconfigurations/apps/v1/deployment.go\ntype DeploymentApplyConfiguration struct {\n    *metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\",inline\"`\n    *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration `json:\"metadata,omitempty\"`\n    Spec *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration `json:\"spec,omitempty\"`\n    Status *DeploymentStatusApplyConfiguration `json:\"status,omitempty\"`\n}\n\nfunc Deployment(name, namespace string) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration {\n    b := &DeploymentApplyConfiguration{}\n    b.WithName(name)\n    b.WithNamespace(namespace)\n    b.WithKind(\"Deployment\")\n    b.WithAPIVersion(\"apps/v1\")\n    return b\n}\n\nfunc (b *DeploymentApplyConfiguration) WithSpec(spec *DeploymentSpecApplyConfiguration) *DeploymentApplyConfiguration {\n    b.Spec = spec\n    return b\n}\n```\n\n### Key Design Decisions\n\n1. **Pointer Fields**: Every field is a pointer (`*DeploymentSpec`). This distinguishes \"user set this to empty\" vs \"user didn't mention it\". Required for partial updates.\n\n2. **JSON Tags Omit Empty**: Pointers marshal with `omitempty`, so unset fields don't appear in the patch. Minimizes patch size.\n\n3. **Nested Types**: Recursive generation for embedded types (specs, metadata, etc.). Each gets its own builder.\n\n4. **Extract Functions**: Reverse operation that parses managed fields and reconstructs the apply configuration for a specific manager. Located at lines 56-100 in deployment.go example.\n\n5. **Blocklisted Fields**: Certain fields are never included:\n   - `ObjectMeta.ManagedFields`: Can't be client-set (generated from merge logic)\n   - `ObjectMeta.SelfLink`: Deprecated, filtered at line 148 in applyconfiguration.go\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Managed Fields and Conflict Handling\n\n### Managed Fields Entry Structure\n\n```yaml\nmetadata:\n  managedFields:\n  - manager: \"my-controller\"\n    operation: \"Apply\"          # or \"Update\"\n    apiVersion: \"apps/v1\"\n    time: \"2024-03-01T12:00:00Z\"\n    fieldsV1:                    # Structured field representation\n      f:spec:\n        f:replicas: {}\n        f:template:\n          f:spec:\n                f:containers:\n                  k:{\"name\":\"app\"}:\n                    f:image: {}\n```\n\n**Manager String**: Identifies the client making the request. Typically includes API version and operation type for deduplication.\n\n**Operation**:\n- `Apply`: From PATCH with ApplyYAMLPatchType; idempotent\n- `Update`: From PUT/POST; overrides previous values\n\n**FieldsV1**: Internal representation using structured-merge-diff's fieldpath.Path API. Each field path is tracked separately.\n\n### Conflict Detection Algorithm\n\n**Trigger**: When `FieldManager.Apply()` is called with `force=false`:\n\n```go\n// managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:160+\nobj, managed, err = f.fieldManager.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)\nif conflict, isConflict := err.(*merge.Conflicts); isConflict && !force {\n    return nil, internal.NewConflictError(conflict)\n}\n```\n\n**Detection**: Delegated to structured-merge-diff:\n1. Decode managed fields from live object (knows current ownership)\n2. For each field in patch:\n   - If owned by a different manager AND value differs → conflict\n3. Return list of conflicting paths and their owners\n\n**Example**:\n- Live: `spec.replicas=3, owned by hpa`\n- Patch: `spec.replicas=5, sent by my-app`\n- Conflict: Path `[spec][replicas]`, manager `hpa`\n\n**Conflict Error**: HTTP 409 with causes per `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"status\": \"Failure\",\n  \"code\": 409,\n  \"reason\": \"Conflict\",\n  \"details\": {\n    \"causes\": [\n      {\n        \"reason\": \"FieldManagerConflict\",\n        \"message\": \"conflict with \\\"hpa\\\"\",\n        \"field\": \"spec.replicas\"\n      }\n    ]\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Force Apply Semantics\n\n**PatchOptions.Force = true** means: \"I acknowledge conflicts and claim disputed fields.\"\n\n**Server behavior**:\n1. Ignores conflicts during merge\n2. Removes conflicting fields from other managers' entries\n3. Adds those fields to requesting manager's entry\n4. Returns 200 OK with modified object\n\n**Critical caveat**: Force apply is **not** a three-way merge. The patch completely replaces fields, not merges them. If patch omits a list, entire list is deleted.\n\n### Backward Compatibility: Last-Applied-Configuration\n\n**Purpose**: kubectl apply traditionally stored `kubectl.kubernetes.io/last-applied-configuration` to compute three-way diffs (local → server → last-known). SSA renders this obsolete but maintains it for compatibility.\n\n**Manager**: `LastAppliedManager` wrapper in managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go\n\n**Behavior**:\n- When Apply operation succeeds, annotation is updated to the patch that was applied\n- Non-Apply operations (PUT) don't modify it\n- Useful for clients that haven't migrated to native SSA\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 7.1 Custom FieldManager Wrappers\n\n**Hook Point**: `NewDefaultFieldManager()` constructor chain at lines 56-74 in managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go.\n\n**Current Wrappers**:\n- **VersionCheckManager**: Validates APIVersion matches expected\n- **LastAppliedUpdater**: Maintains last-applied-configuration annotation\n- **ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager**: Optimization to skip merge processing for non-apply operations with probability DefaultTrackOnCreateProbability (1.0 by default)\n- **CapManagersManager**: Limits number of tracked managers to prevent unbounded growth\n\n**Extension Pattern**:\n```go\ntype CustomManager struct {\n    wrapped Manager\n}\n\nfunc (m *CustomManager) Update(liveObj, newObj runtime.Object, managed Managed, manager string) (object runtime.Object, managed Managed, err error) {\n    // custom logic before\n    object, managed, err = m.wrapped.Update(liveObj, newObj, managed, manager)\n    // custom logic after\n    return\n}\n```\n\n**Use Case**: Audit field changes, enforce naming conventions, inject standard labels/annotations.\n\n### 7.2 TypeConverter Customization\n\n**Location**: managedfields/typeconverter.go\n\n**Interface**:\n```go\ntype TypeConverter interface {\n    Convert(obj interface{}, typeFQN string) (*value.Value, error)\n    ObjectToTyped(obj runtime.Object) (*value.Value, error)\n    TypedToObject(val *value.Value) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Default**: Uses `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.DefaultUnstructuredConverter` to convert typed objects to unstructured maps.\n\n**Extension**: CRDs can provide custom converters to handle non-standard types.\n\n### 7.3 Schema Definition: OpenAPI Integration\n\n**Purpose**: Structured-merge-diff uses OpenAPI schemas to understand field types (maps, lists, scalars). This enables proper merge semantics:\n- Map fields: Merge recursively\n- List fields with merge keys: Reorder/dedup by key\n- Scalar fields: Replace atomically\n\n**In Kubernetes**:\n- Built-in types: Schema inferred from Go structs (via OpenAPI gen)\n- CRDs: Schema defined in `spec.validation.openAPIV3Schema`\n\n**If schema missing**: Fallback to \"unknown type\" merge (treats all values as scalars, no recursion).\n\n### 7.4 Managed Fields Reset: Field Filters\n\n**Location**: managedfields/fieldmanager.go:36-52 (resetFields parameter)\n\n**Purpose**: On resource creation, exclude certain fields from being tracked (e.g., status subresources).\n\n**API**:\n```go\nresetFields map[fieldpath.APIVersion]fieldpath.Filter\n\n// Example: status fields not tracked on create\nresetFields[v1.APIVersion] = filter matching \"status\" fields\n```\n\n**Effect**: Fields in resetFields start unowned; any manager setting them later claims them cleanly.\n\n**Use Case**: Status subresources should be owned by status controllers, not regular managers.\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Failure Modes, Limits, and Tradeoffs\n\n### 8.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Managed Fields Corruption by Admission\n\n**Problem**: Mutating admission webhooks may modify objects in ways that corrupt managed fields.\n\n**Mitigation** (fieldmanager/admission.go): Wrapper validates managed fields after each admission pass. If invalid, **reverts** to pre-admission state and adds warning.\n\n**Limitation**: Validation only catches structural corruption (invalid JSON in fieldsV1). Webhooks can still add fields that bypass field ownership checks.\n\n#### Unbounded Manager Count\n\n**Problem**: If many different clients apply to same resource, managed fields grows without bound.\n\n**Mitigation** (CapManagersManager): Limit to DefaultMaxUpdateManagers=10. Older Update entries are merged (combined).\n\n**Limitation**: Compressed history loses field ownership details for old managers. After compression, can't extract precise previous configurations.\n\n**Impact**: If >10 controllers touch a resource, some history is lost.\n\n#### Conflict on Apply with Small Patch\n\n**Problem**: User applies a partial patch that conflicts with another controller's full specification.\n\n**Example**:\n```yaml\n# Controller A owns full Pod spec\n# User tries to apply just image: \"v2\"\n# But controller A had image: \"v1\"\n# Conflict on image!\n```\n\n**Solution**: Force-apply, but only if intentional.\n\n**Limitation**: Force-apply is all-or-nothing. Can't force specific fields.\n\n#### Schema Mismatch with CRDs\n\n**Problem**: CRD schema changes (list field becomes map), but old managed fields still reference old structure.\n\n**Mitigation**: If schema can't be found during merge, falls back to scalar merge (no recursion).\n\n**Limitation**: Older managed fields entries for pre-schema-change structure become stale.\n\n#### Lost Updates via GuaranteedUpdate Retry\n\n**Problem**: HTTP request timeout during GuaranteedUpdate retry loop.\n\n**Mitigation** (patch.go:734-736): If timeout error received, server can't guarantee whether object was persisted.\n\n**Behavior**: Returns 504 Gateway Timeout. Client must retry with awareness that object may have been created.\n\n**Limitation**: No way to know if partial application succeeded. Requires idempotent apply semantics.\n\n### 8.2 Limits\n\n| Limit | Value | Location | Note |\n|-------|-------|----------|------|\n| Max JSON Patch operations | 10,000 | patch.go:64 | Per RFC 6902 |\n| Max Update managers | 10 | managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go:35 | Older entries merged |\n| Max request body size | Configurable (default 3MB) | handlers/patch.go:110 | Via apiserver flag |\n| Max field path depth | Unbounded | structured-merge-diff | Theoretical limit depends on memory |\n| Managed fields JSON size | Unbounded | Storage | Large numbers of managers → larger objects |\n\n### 8.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Field-Level vs. Resource-Level Ownership\n\n**Choice**: Kubernetes uses field-level tracking.\n\n**Pro**: Multiple controllers can co-manage same resource at different fields. HPA sets replicas, user manages selector.\n\n**Con**: Adds complexity, requires schema understanding, merge logic more intricate.\n\n**Alternative**: Resource-level (last-write-wins). Simpler but forces exclusive ownership.\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Three-Way Merge vs. Two-Way\n\n**Choice**: Kubernetes uses two-way merge (current state + patch), reconstructs previous state from managed fields.\n\n**Pro**: Doesn't require client to send three-way state, reduces API complexity.\n\n**Con**: Reconstructed \"previous\" state may be incomplete (other managers may have modified fields).\n\n**Example**:\n```\nLive state:  replicas=5, owned by HPA\nPatch:       replicas=3, sent by user\nReconstructed \"previous\" from managed fields: HPA owns replicas (assumed value is 5)\nMerge result: Conflict (HPA disagrees with user's 3)\n```\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: Force-Apply Atomicity\n\n**Choice**: Force-apply claims all fields in patch, not selective.\n\n**Pro**: Simple to implement, clear semantics.\n\n**Con**: Can't force-apply specific fields, must accept all-or-nothing.\n\n**Workaround**: Extract, modify specific fields, reapply (avoids conflicts).\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Manager String Format\n\n**Choice**: Opaque JSON string containing { manager, operation, apiVersion }.\n\n**Pro**: Extensible, can add fields for future needs.\n\n**Con**: Not human-readable, requires JSON parsing to inspect.\n\n**Alternative**: Structured tuple (manager, op, version).\n\n---\n\n## Part 9: Operational Implications\n\n### 9.1 Performance Impact\n\n#### Apply Patch Processing\n\n**Cost**: Structured-merge-diff three-way merge is O(n) in live object size and patch size.\n\n**Optimization 1** (ProbabilisticSkipNonAppliedManager): For non-Apply operations, skip merge if fields are likely untouched (configurable probability, default 100% skip).\n\n**Optimization 2** (CapManagersManager): Merge old Update entries to keep manager count low.\n\n**Optimization 3** (patch.go:713-726): If object too large, retry after removing managedFields. Managed fields can be >100KB on large objects with many managers.\n\n**Result**: First few applies are slow (merge), subsequent non-apply updates are fast (skip).\n\n#### Managed Fields Storage Overhead\n\n**Typical**: 0.5-2KB per managed entry, depends on number of fields tracked.\n\n**Large scale**: 10 managers × 500 fields average = ~5KB managed fields metadata.\n\n**Impact**: Cluster with 10,000 Pods × 5KB = 50MB total managed fields metadata in etcd.\n\n**Mitigation**: Regularly delete old/unused controllers to keep manager count low.\n\n### 9.2 Debugging and Troubleshooting\n\n#### Inspect Managed Fields\n\n```bash\nkubectl get pod <name> -o yaml | grep -A 50 \"managedFields:\"\n```\n\nShows which manager owns which fields, when last modified.\n\n#### Extract Configuration\n\n```bash\n# Extract what \"my-app\" manager owns\nkubectl get deployment <name> -o yaml | \\\n  jq '.metadata.managedFields[] | select(.manager==\"my-app\")'\n```\n\nHelps understand what a controller thinks it should own.\n\n#### Conflict Resolution\n\n```bash\n# Check conflict details\nkubectl apply -f config.yaml 2>&1 | grep \"conflict with\"\n\n# Force apply to claim fields\nkubectl apply -f config.yaml --field-manager=my-app --force-conflicts\n```\n\n#### Manager Cleanup\n\n```bash\n# List active managers on a resource\nkubectl patch deployment <name> --type='json' -p='[{\"op\":\"test\",\"path\":\"/metadata/managedFields\"}]'\n\n# Manually clear stale manager (CAUTION: only if manager is truly abandoned)\nkubectl patch deployment <name> --type='json' \\\n  -p='[{\"op\":\"remove\",\"path\":\"/metadata/managedFields/0\"}]'\n```\n\n### 9.3 Migration Considerations\n\n#### From Traditional PUT/POST to Apply\n\n**Challenge**: Existing resources have no managed fields. First apply sees all fields as unowned.\n\n**Mitigation**: Initial apply claims all fields:\n```bash\nkubectl apply -f existing-resource.yaml --field-manager=new-manager --force-conflicts\n```\n\n**Result**: Migrates resource to SSA model.\n\n#### From Client-Side Apply to Server-Side Apply\n\n**Tool**: `kubectl apply --server-side` (requires cluster v1.18+).\n\n**Process**:\n1. Read current state (live object + managedFields)\n2. Extract last-applied-configuration annotation\n3. Compute three-way diff (last → live → desired)\n4. Send as apply PATCH\n5. Server merges with other manager changes\n\n**Compatibility**: Server-side apply is backward compatible; old resources automatically gain managed fields.\n\n#### Multi-Version Controller Rollout\n\n**Scenario**: Rolling out new version of controller with different field ownership.\n\n**Approach**:\n1. Old and new versions coexist (different manager strings, e.g., \"my-controller:v1\" vs \"my-controller:v2\")\n2. Each manages same fields but with different manager names\n3. On rollout: New version applies same fields, old version's entries become stale\n4. After stabilization: Run cleanup to merge old manager entries\n\n**Caution**: If both versions apply simultaneously, conflicts arise until old version is deleted.\n\n### 9.4 Reliability and Data Consistency\n\n#### Idempotency\n\n**Property**: Applying same configuration multiple times produces same result.\n\n**Guaranteed by**: Apply with same field values always succeeds (no conflict on identical fields).\n\n**Exception**: External changes (e.g., HPA sets replicas differently) cause conflicts on next apply.\n\n**Implication**: Controllers can safely retry apply on transient errors without duplicating side effects.\n\n#### Observability\n\n**What's Tracked**:\n- Each managed field's owner, timestamp, operation\n- **Not tracked**: When fields were set, intermediate values, change history\n\n**Limitation**: Can't audit \"who changed field X on date Y\" without reading etcd snapshots.\n\n**Alternative**: Use Kubernetes audit logging (separate system) to track API requests.\n\n#### Quota and Accounting\n\n**Managed Fields Count Toward**:\n- Resource size (quota.requests.storage)\n- **Not counted separately**: No per-manager quota\n\n**Implication**: Unbounded managers on single object can bloat resource size, potentially hitting quotas.\n\n**Mitigation**: Enforce application-level manager naming standards, cleanup old managers.\n\n---\n\n## Part 10: Conclusion\n\nServer-Side Apply is a sophisticated system that enables safe, declarative configuration management in Kubernetes by tracking field ownership at the API server level. Its key innovation is moving from \"last-write-wins\" to \"field-level ownership,\" allowing multiple controllers to coexist on the same resource.\n\nThe subsystem achieves this through:\n\n1. **ApplyConfigurations**: Type-safe builders generated for every API type, enabling clients to construct apply patches without raw YAML\n2. **FieldManager**: Orchestrates merge logic, decodes/encodes managed fields, wraps with optimization and validation layers\n3. **Structured-Merge-Diff**: External library implementing field ownership semantics and conflict detection\n4. **HTTP Handler**: Routes PATCH requests with apply content-type to the merge pipeline\n5. **Managed Fields Metadata**: Tracks per-field ownership, operation type, and timestamp in API objects\n\nUnderstanding this system enables:\n- Effective multi-controller resource management\n- Predictable conflict resolution\n- Safe schema evolution\n- Operational debugging of ownership disputes\n- Integration of new controllers without breaking existing ones\n\nThe design prioritizes **safety over simplicity**: field-level tracking and structured merge logic add complexity but prevent whole categories of data loss and ownership conflicts that plagued earlier Kubernetes versions.\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
